<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="kmtc-med-surg-1-medical-surgical-nursing-notes">KMTC MED SURG 1 - Medical surgical nursing notes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#kmtc-med-surg-1-medical-surgical-nursing-notes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Kenya Registered Community Health Nursing (Kenya Medical Training College)</p>

<p>MARCH 2024</p>
<p>MEDICAL SURGICAL NURSING 1</p>
<p>CODE: MSN 1202.</p>
<p>Lecturer: Ms. Jeniffer K. Musyoka</p>
<p>HOURS:16</p>
<p>Course purpose: This course prepares the student/learner to apply theoretical knowledge and basic nursing skills when providing care in meeting the biopsychosocial needs of adult clients with simple/common medical and surgical problems.</p>
<p>MODULE UNITS.</p>
<ol>
<li>Basic concepts in medical surgical nursing-2 hours</li>
<li>Classification of diseases-2 hours</li>
<li>Medical surgical conditions-4 hours</li>
<li>Burns-6 hours.</li>
</ol>
<p>Module content</p>
<ol>
<li>basic concepts in medical surgical nursing: definitions, history of medicine and surgery, the process of inflammation.</li>
<li>Classification of diseases: genetic, bacterial, viral. Neoplasmic (benign and malignant), traumatic</li>
<li>medical surgical conditions: cellulitis, boils, septicemia, abscesses, wound healing, fluid and electrolyte imbalance, acid base imbalance, shock</li>
<li>Burns: types of burns (thermal, chemical, electrical, friction, radiation), classification of burns (first, second and third degree burns), local and systemic responses to burns, management of burn injuries (resuscitative, acute phase) rehabilitation.</li>
</ol>
<p>BASIC CONCEPTS IN MEDICAL-SURGICAL NURSING</p>
<p>Definitions:</p>
<ul>
<li>Medical-Surgical Nursing:</li>
</ul>
<p>Definition: A specialized area of nursing practice that focuses on the care of adult patients undergoing surgery or medical treatment.</p>
<p>Scope: It includes</p>
<p>&gt; Surgical Care: management of diseases and conditions through operative procedures. It involves the use of surgical techniques to diagnose, treat, or manage medical conditions that cannot be addressed through non-surgical means. Surgical care can be classified into different types based on the urgency and nature of the procedure.</p>
<p>This document is available on
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Elective Surgery: Planned surgeries that are not urgently needed but are performed to improve the patient's quality of life or manage a condition that is not life-threatening. e.g. Appendectomy (removal of the appendix for appendicitis) Cosmetic Surgery (e.g., breast augmentation, rhinoplasty)</p>
<p>Emergency Surgery: Unplanned surgeries required to address acute medical conditions that pose an immediate risk to the patient's life or health. E.g. Emergency C-Section (for complications during childbirth)</p>
<ul>
<li>Preoperative Care: refers to the period leading up to a surgical procedure. It involves preparing the patient both physically and psychologically for surgery.</li>
<li>Intraoperative Care: Definition: encompasses the management and monitoring of the patient during the actual surgical procedure.</li>
<li>Postoperative Care: care provided after surgery to support recovery, manage complications, and ensure a smooth transition from the operating room to recovery.</li>
</ul>
<p>Management of Medical Conditions.</p>
<ul>
<li>Chronic Conditions: are long-term health issues that require ongoing management and care. E.g. Diabetes, hypertension,</li>
<li>Acute Conditions: are sudden or severe health issues that require immediate attention. E.g. Acute myocardial infarction (heart attack),</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="concepts-of-health-and-illnesses">CONCEPTS OF HEALTH AND ILLNESSES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#concepts-of-health-and-illnesses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-definition-of-health">1. Definition of Health<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-definition-of-health" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>World Health Organization (WHO) Definition:</li>
</ul>
<p>Health: The WHO defines health as "a state of complete physical, mental, and social well-being, and not merely the absence of disease or infirmity."</p>
<p>This broad definition emphasizes that health is more than just the absence of illness; it includes overall well-being and quality of life.</p>
<ul>
<li>Holistic Approach:</li>
</ul>
<p>Physical Health: Involves the proper functioning of the body's systems and the absence of disease or injury.</p>
<p>Mental Health: Refers to emotional and psychological well-being, including the ability to manage stress, relate to others, and make decisions.</p>
<p>Social Health: Encompasses the quality of relationships and social support systems, including the ability to interact and form meaningful connections with others.</p>
<ul>
<li>Dimensions of Health:</li>
</ul>
<p>Physical: Fitness, nutrition, and absence of illness.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Mental: Cognitive function, emotional regulation, and mental health conditions.</p>
<p>Social: Social relationships, community involvement, and support systems.</p>
<p>Spiritual: Sense of purpose, belonging, and spiritual practices.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-definition-of-illness">2. Definition of Illness<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-definition-of-illness" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Illness refers to the subjective experience of symptoms and suffering, as perceived by the individual. It encompasses how a person feels and how they interpret their health status. Unlike disease, which is an objective pathological condition, illness is the personal experience of the impact of disease.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="disease">Disease:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disease" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Disease refers to a pathological condition of a bodily part, an organism, or system resulting from various causes, such as infection, genetic defect, or environmental factors, and characterized by an identifiable group of signs or symptoms. It is often diagnosed by medical professionals based on clinical and laboratory findings.</p>
<p>Acute vs. Chronic Illness: Acute Illness: Sudden onset, severe symptoms, and often short duration. Example: Influenza, appendicitis.</p>
<p>Chronic Illness: Long-lasting, often persistent over a lifetime, and may have periods of exacerbation and remission. Example: Diabetes, hypertension</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-history-of-medicine-and-surgery">2. HISTORY OF MEDICINE AND SURGERY:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-history-of-medicine-and-surgery" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Ancient Medicine and Surgery:</li>
</ul>
<p>Early Practices: Ancient civilizations, such as the Egyptians, Greeks, and Chinese, practiced various forms of medicine and surgery. Techniques included herbal remedies, trepanation (drilling holes in the skull), and rudimentary surgical procedures.</p>
<p>Notable Figures:</p>
<p>Hippocrates (460–370 BC): Often referred to as the "Father of Medicine," Hippocrates is known for his contributions to clinical medicine and the Hippocratic Oath.</p>
<p>Galen (129–200 AD): A prominent Greek physician whose writings dominated medical knowledge in Europe for over a millennium.</p>
<ul>
<li>Middle Ages:</li>
</ul>
<p>Medical Advancements: During the medieval period, medical knowledge was preserved and expanded by Islamic scholars. Key figures included Avicenna (Ibn Sina), who wrote "The Canon of Medicine," which was influential in both the Islamic world and Europe.</p>
<p>Surgical Practices: Surgery was often performed by barbers or barber-surgeons, who were less formally trained compared to physicians.</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>s  t  u  d  o  c  u</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Renaissance:</li>
</ul>
<p>Medical Renaissance: The Renaissance period saw a revival of scientific inquiry and advancement in medical knowledge. Figures like Andreas Vesalius challenged existing anatomical knowledge with detailed dissections and accurate anatomical drawings.</p>
<p>Surgical Innovations: Ambroise Paré, a pioneering French surgeon, made significant contributions to surgical techniques and wound care.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>19th Century:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Advancements in Surgery: The development of anesthesia and antiseptic techniques revolutionized surgery.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Anesthesia: The use of ether and chloroform allowed for pain-free surgeries.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Antiseptics: Joseph Lister’s work on antiseptic techniques reduced surgical infections and improved patient outcomes.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Medical Education: The establishment of modern medical schools and residency programs helped standardize medical and surgical training.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>20th and 21st Centuries:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Technological Advances: Innovations such as endoscopic surgery, minimally invasive techniques, and advanced imaging (e.g., MRI, CT scans) have dramatically improved surgical outcomes and patient care.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Evidence-Based Practice: The emphasis on evidence-based practice has led to the development of guidelines and protocols that enhance patient safety and care quality.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Integrated Care: The focus has shifted towards a multidisciplinary approach to patient care, integrating medical, surgical, and nursing interventions.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>PROCESS OF INFLAMMATION</p>
<ol>
<li>Definition of Inflammation</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Inflammation: A complex biological response of tissues to harmful stimuli such as pathogens, damaged cells, or irritants. It is a protective mechanism intended to remove the harmful stimuli and initiate the healing process. Inflammation can be classified into acute and chronic types.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="2">
<li>Types of Inflammation</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Acute Inflammation: Short-term response to injury or infection, typically lasting a few days to a couple of weeks. It is characterized by redness, heat, swelling, pain, and loss of function.</li>
<li>Chronic Inflammation: Long-term inflammation lasting for months or years. It often results from persistent infections, autoimmune disorders, or chronic exposure to irritants.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Chronic inflammation can lead to tissue damage and contribute to various diseases such as arthritis, cardiovascular disease, and cancer.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-stages-of-acute-inflammation">3. Stages of Acute Inflammation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-stages-of-acute-inflammation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="1-vascular-stage">1. Vascular Stage:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-vascular-stage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li><strong>Vasodilation</strong>: The initial response involves the widening of blood vessels to increase blood flow to the affected area. This leads to redness (erythema) and warmth.</li>
<li><strong>Increased Permeability</strong>: The blood vessel walls become more permeable, allowing fluids, proteins, and white blood cells to pass through and enter the tissue. This results in swelling (edema).</li>
<li><strong>Formation of Exudate</strong>: The fluid that accumulates in the tissues, known as exudate, consists of plasma, proteins (such as fibrin), and leukocytes (white blood cells).</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="2-cellular-stage">2. Cellular Stage:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-cellular-stage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li><strong>Leukocyte Migration</strong>: White blood cells (mainly neutrophils) move towards the site of injury or infection. This process is guided by chemical signals known as chemotactic factors.</li>
<li><strong>Phagocytosis</strong>: Neutrophils and other phagocytes (such as macrophages) engulf and digest pathogens, dead cells, and debris. This process helps to clear the harmful agents and facilitate tissue repair.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="3-resolution-stage">3. Resolution Stage:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-resolution-stage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li><strong>Cessation of Inflammation</strong>: Once the harmful stimuli are removed, the inflammatory response is downregulated. Anti-inflammatory signals and mediators help to resolve the inflammation.</li>
<li><strong>Repair and Healing</strong>: Tissue repair involves the replacement of damaged cells with new cells, tissue regeneration, or scar formation. Fibroblasts play a key role in this phase by producing collagen and extracellular matrix components.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="key-mediators-of-inflammation">Key Mediators of Inflammation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#key-mediators-of-inflammation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li><strong>Chemical Mediators</strong>: Various substances are involved in the inflammatory response, including:</li>
<li><strong>Histamine</strong>: Released by mast cells, histamine causes vasodilation and increased vascular permeability.</li>
<li><strong>Prostaglandins</strong>: Produced by damaged cells, these mediators contribute to pain, fever, and increased blood flow.</li>
<li><strong>Leukotrienes</strong>: Involved in the recruitment and activation of leukocytes.</li>
</ul>

<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Cytokines: Proteins such as interleukins (IL) and tumor necrosis factor (TNF) that regulate the intensity and duration of inflammation.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cellular-mediators">Cellular Mediators:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cellular-mediators" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Neutrophils: The first responders to infection or injury, responsible for phagocytosing pathogens and debris.</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Macrophages: These cells follow neutrophils and play a role in phagocytosis, tissue repair, and secretion of cytokines.</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Mast Cells: Found in connective tissues, they release histamine and other mediators during the early inflammatory response.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-signs-of-inflammation">Clinical Signs of Inflammation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-signs-of-inflammation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Redness (Erythema): Increased blood flow to the affected area.</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Heat (Hyperthermia): Elevated blood flow and metabolic activity.</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Swelling (Edema): Accumulation of fluid in the interstitial spaces.</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Pain (Dolor): Release of chemical mediators that stimulate pain receptors.</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Loss of Function (Functio Laesa): Reduced ability to use the affected body part due to pain and swelling.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="systemic-responses-to-inflammation">Systemic Responses to Inflammation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#systemic-responses-to-inflammation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Fever: A common systemic response, often caused by the release of pyrogens (fever-inducing substances) that affect the hypothalamus.</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Leukocytosis: An increase in white blood cells in the blood, indicating an inflammatory response.</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Acute Phase Response: Includes changes in blood plasma proteins such as C-reactive protein (CRP) and fibrinogen, which are produced in response to inflammation.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="chronic-inflammation">Chronic Inflammation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chronic-inflammation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Causes: Persistent infections, autoimmune diseases, prolonged exposure to irritants, or unresolved acute inflammation.</li>
<li>Characteristics: Infiltration of mononuclear cells (macrophages, lymphocytes), tissue destruction, and attempted repair involving fibrosis and angiogenesis.</li>
<li>Diseases Associated: Rheumatoid arthritis, inflammatory bowel disease, atherosclerosis, and chronic obstructive pulmonary disease (COPD).</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-inflammation">Management of Inflammation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-inflammation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>a) Pharmacologic Treatments:</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>✓ Nonsteroidal Anti-Inflammatory Drugs (NSAIDs): Reduce pain, fever, and inflammation by inhibiting prostaglandin synthesis (e.g., ibuprofen, aspirin).
✓ Corticosteroids: Potent anti-inflammatory agents that suppress the immune response (e.g., prednisone).
✓ Disease-Modifying Antirheumatic Drugs (DMARDs): Used in chronic inflammatory conditions like rheumatoid arthritis to modify disease progression (e.g., methotrexate).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="b-non-pharmacologic-treatments">b) Non-Pharmacologic Treatments:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-non-pharmacologic-treatments" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>✓ Rest and Elevation: Reduces swelling and promotes healing.
✓ Ice and Heat Therapy: Ice reduces inflammation and pain, while heat can relax muscles and improve blood flow.
✓ Physical Therapy: Assists in restoring function and mobility.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="c-lifestyle-modifications">c) Lifestyle Modifications:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#c-lifestyle-modifications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>✓ Diet: Anti-inflammatory diets rich in fruits, vegetables, and omega-3 fatty acids.
✓ Exercise: Regular physical activity can help manage chronic inflammation and improve overall health.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="complications-of-inflammation">Complications of Inflammation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications-of-inflammation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>✓ Tissue Damage: Persistent inflammation can lead to damage of healthy tissues and organs.
✓ Scarring and Fibrosis: Chronic inflammation may result in scar formation and loss of normal tissue function.
✓ Increased Risk of Chronic Diseases: Long-term inflammation is associated with diseases such as cardiovascular disease, diabetes, and cancer</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="wound-healing">WOUND HEALING<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#wound-healing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types-of-wounds">Types of Wounds<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-wounds" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>➤ Acute Wounds: result from trauma, surgery, or injury. These wounds progress through the normal stages of healing.</p>
<p>Examples: Surgical incisions, lacerations, abrasions.</p>
<p>➤ Chronic Wounds: Do not progress through the normal stages of healing and may remain in the inflammatory or proliferative phase for extended periods.</p>
<ul>
<li>Examples: Pressure ulcers, venous ulcers, diabetic foot ulcers.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="classification-of-wounds">Classification of wounds<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification-of-wounds" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This document is available on
5
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ol>
<li>by degree of contamination</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>clean
uninfected wounds in which no inflammation is encountered and the respiratory, gastrointestinal, genital, and/or urinary tracts are not entered</li>
<li>clean/contaminated
uninfected wounds in which no inflammation is encountered but the respiratory, gastrointestinal, genital, and/or urinary tract have been entered</li>
<li>contaminated
open, traumatic wounds or surgical wounds involving a major break in sterile technique that show evidence of inflammation</li>
<li>infected
old, traumatic wounds containing dead tissue and wounds with evidence of a clinical infection (e.g., purulent drainage)</li>
</ul>
<ol start="2">
<li>by depth</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>partial-thickness
involves only the epidermal and dermal layers of skin</li>
<li>full-thickness
involves the epidermal and dermal layers of skin, subcutaneous tissue and, possibly, muscle and bone</li>
</ul>
<ol start="3">
<li>by descriptive qualities</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>laceration
involves tearing apart of tissues resulting in irregular wound edges</li>
<li>abrasion
involves scraping or rubbing the surface of the skin by friction</li>
<li>contusion
involves a blow from a blunt object resulting in swelling, discoloration, bruising, and/or ec Cymosis</li>
<li>incision
involves cutting the skin with a sharp instrument</li>
<li>puncture
involves penetration of the skin and, often, the underlying tissues by a sharp instrument</li>
</ul>
<p>Types of wound discharges</p>
<ul>
<li>serous exudate
consists chiefly of serum derived from blood and serous membranes of the body</li>
<li>sanguineous
consists of serum and red blood cells</li>
<li>purulent
consists of serum and pus (leukocytes, liquefied living and dead bacteria, dead tissue debris)</li>
</ul>
<p>Types of wound healing</p>
<ul>
<li>Healing by primary intention
occurs in wounds with dermal edges that are close together (e.g a scalpel incision).</li>
</ul>
<p>wound is closed using staples, stitches, glues, or other forms of wound-closing processes.</p>
<p>This reduces the tissue lost and allows the body to focus on closing and healing a smaller-area wound rather than the larger initial wound</p>
<p>It is usually faster than by secondary intention</p>
<p>The end result of healing by primary intention is (in most cases) a complete return to function, with minimal scarring and loss of skin appendages</p>
<ul>
<li>Secondary Intention</li>
</ul>
<p>occurs when the sides of the wound are not opposed, therefore healing must occur from the bottom of the wound upwards.</p>
<p>the wound that cannot be stitched because of a large amount of tissue loss.</p>
<p>relies on the body's own healing mechanisms.</p>
<p>This process takes longer, which may be due to increased wound size, the risk of infection and contamination, and other factors, such as the use of certain medications</p>
<p>A complication from wound healing (particularly in people with darker skin), are keloid scars, whereby there is excessive collagen production, leading to extensive scarring. This can occur in both primary and secondary intention healing</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Tertiary wound healing</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>healing by delayed primary closure, occurs when there is a need to delay the wound-closing process.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>E.g. infectious germs in a wound . allow the wound to drain or wait for the effects of other therapies to take place before closing the wound.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Stages of Wound Healing</li>
</ol>
<p>Wound healing occurs in four overlapping phases: hemostasis, inflammation, proliferation, and remodeling.</p>
<ol>
<li>Hemostasis (Immediate Response)</li>
</ol>
<p>Duration: Minutes to hours post-injury.</p>
<p>It is characterized by:</p>
<p>✓ Vascular Constriction: Immediate constriction of blood vessels reduces blood flow to the wound area.
✓ Platelet Aggregation: Platelets adhere to the damaged tissue and each other, forming a platelet plug to stop bleeding.
✓ Clot Formation: The clotting cascade is activated, leading to fibrin clot formation, which serves as a temporary barrier and matrix for incoming cells.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-inflammation-cleaning-up">2. Inflammation (Cleaning Up)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-inflammation-cleaning-up" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Duration: Days 1-4.</li>
</ul>
<p>It is characterized by:</p>
<ul>
<li>☑ Vasodilation: Blood vessels dilate to increase blood flow to the area, allowing immune cells to access the wound.</li>
<li>☑ Leukocyte Infiltration: Neutrophils are the first cells to arrive, followed by macrophages. They phagocytize debris, pathogens, and damaged cells.</li>
<li>☑ Cytokine Release: Pro-inflammatory cytokines are released, coordinating the inflammatory response and preparing the wound bed for repair.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-3-proliferation-rebuilding">1.3 Proliferation (Rebuilding)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-3-proliferation-rebuilding" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Duration: Days 4-21.</li>
</ul>
<p>It is characterized by:</p>
<ul>
<li>☑ Angiogenesis: Formation of new blood vessels from existing vessels to supply oxygen and nutrients to the healing tissue.</li>
<li>☑ Fibroplasia: Fibroblasts proliferate and synthesize collagen and extracellular matrix, providing structural support.</li>
<li>☑ Re-epithelialization: Keratinocytes migrate across the wound bed, covering it with new epithelial tissue.</li>
<li>☑ Wound Contraction: Myofibroblasts pull the edges of the wound together, reducing its size.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-remodeling-maturation">.4 Remodeling (Maturation)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-remodeling-maturation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Duration: Weeks to years.</li>
</ul>
<p>It is characterized by:</p>
<ul>
<li>☑ Collagen Remodeling: Type III collagen is gradually replaced by Type I collagen, increasing tensile strength of the wound.</li>
<li>☑ Matrix Remodeling: The extracellular matrix is reorganized and strengthened.</li>
<li>☑ Scar Formation: The final scar is less elastic and has fewer sweat glands and hair follicles compared to the surrounding skin.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="factors-affecting-wound-healing">Factors Affecting Wound Healing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#factors-affecting-wound-healing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Local Factors:</p>
<ul>
<li>☑ Infection: Presence of pathogens can prolong inflammation and impair healing.</li>
<li>☑ Necrotic Tissue: Dead tissue must be removed for healing to progress.</li>
<li>☑ Wound Oxygenation: Adequate oxygen supply is essential for cellular functions and collagen synthesis.</li>
</ul>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Size and depth of wound.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="systemic-factors">Systemic Factors:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#systemic-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Nutrition: Adequate intake of proteins, vitamins (especially Vitamin C and A), and minerals (such as zinc) is essential for healing.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Chronic Diseases: Conditions like diabetes, vascular disease, and immunosuppression can delay healing.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Medications: Certain drugs, such as corticosteroids and immunosuppressants, can impair the healing process.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="lifestyle-factors">Lifestyle Factors:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#lifestyle-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Smoking: Nicotine constricts blood vessels and impairs oxygen delivery to the wound site.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Alcohol Use: Excessive alcohol can affect immune function and delay healing.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="wound-management-principles">Wound Management Principles<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#wound-management-principles" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="i-assessment">I. Assessment:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#i-assessment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Wound Type: Identify whether the wound is acute or chronic.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Wound Bed: Evaluate for signs of infection, necrosis, and tissue viability.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Surrounding Skin: Check for signs of maceration, irritation, or infection.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="ii-cleaning">II. Cleaning:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ii-cleaning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Wound Cleansing: Use appropriate solutions (e.g., saline, antiseptic solutions) to clean the wound without damaging healthy tissue.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Debridement: Remove necrotic tissue and foreign bodies to promote healing.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="iii-dressing">III. Dressing:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#iii-dressing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Wound Protection: Use dressings that maintain a moist environment, absorb exudate, and protect the wound from contaminants.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Types of Dressings: Options include hydrocolloids, hydrogels, alginates, and foams. Selection depends on the wound type and exudate level.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="iv-infection-control">IV. Infection Control:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#iv-infection-control" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Antiseptics: Apply topical antibiotics or antiseptics if infection is suspected or confirmed.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Systemic Antibiotics: Prescribed based on culture and sensitivity results if systemic infection is present.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="v-patient-education">V. Patient Education:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#v-patient-education" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
