<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Vasopressors: Such as norepinephrine or epinephrine, to manage severe hypotension if fluid resuscitation is inadequate.</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Administer prescribed antibiotics: Empirical Antibiotics: Broad-spectrum antibiotics are initially administered while waiting for culture results. Source Control:</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Surgical Intervention: To drain abscesses or remove infected tissues.</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Removal of Invasive Devices: If the infection is associated with devices like central lines.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="7-complications">7. Complications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7-complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Septic Shock: A severe form of sepsis with persistent hypotension despite fluid resuscitation.</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Organ Failure: Including acute respiratory distress syndrome (ARDS), acute kidney injury (AKI), and hepatic dysfunction.</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Disseminated Intravascular Coagulation (DIC): A condition characterized by widespread clotting leading to bleeding complications.</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Long-Term Sequelae: Such as chronic fatigue, cognitive impairments, or post-sepsis syndrome.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="8-prevention">8. Prevention<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#8-prevention" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Infection Control:</li>
</ul>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Hygiene Practices: Proper hand washing and use of personal protective equipment (PPE).</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Sterile Techniques: During invasive procedures to prevent infections.</p>
<ul>
<li>Vaccination:</li>
</ul>
<p>Vaccines: Such as those for influenza and pneumococcal infections, to reduce the risk of infections that can lead to sepsis.</p>
<ul>
<li>Early Detection and Treatment:</li>
</ul>
<p>Prompt Antibiotic Administration: Timely initiation of antibiotics to prevent progression from localized infection to sepsis.</p>
<p>Monitoring High-Risk Patients: Regular assessment of patients with known risk factors for early signs of sepsis.</p>
<ul>
<li>Prognosis: Varies depending on the severity of the sepsis, underlying health conditions, and response to treatment. Early and effective treatment improves outcomes</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="abscesses">ABSCESSES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#abscesses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>An abscess is a localized collection of pus that forms within a tissue, organ, or body space due to infection.</p>
<p>It is typically surrounded by inflamed tissue, known as the abscess wall, which serves to isolate the infection.</p>
<p>Abscesses can occur in any part of the body and vary in size and severity.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-etiology">2. Etiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-etiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="causative-agents">Causative Agents:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causative-agents" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>a) Bacteria: The most common cause of abscesses is bacterial infection. Key pathogens include: Staphylococcus aureus, Streptococcus species: Such as Streptococcus pyogenes, Anaerobes: Such as Bacteroides species.</p>
<p>b) Fungi: Less common but can cause abscesses in immunocompromised individuals. Examples include Candida species.</p>
<p>c) Parasites: Certain parasitic infections can also lead to abscess formation, such as those caused by Entamoeba histolytica (amoebic liver abscess).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="pathogenesis">Pathogenesis:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathogenesis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Infection Entry: Pathogens enter through breaks in the skin, surgical wounds, or via hematogenous spread (from other infections or systemic infection).</li>
<li>Inflammatory Response: The body’s immune response to the infection results in the accumulation of neutrophils, dead cells, and bacteria, forming pus.</li>
<li>Abscess Formation: The body forms a protective barrier around the infection site, leading to the formation of a cavity filled with pus.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-risk-factors">3. Risk Factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-risk-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Skin Injuries: Cuts, wounds, or surgical procedures that disrupt the skin barrier.</li>
<li>Chronic Conditions: Such as diabetes mellitus, which can impair wound healing and immune response.</li>
<li>Immune Suppression: Due to conditions like HIV/AIDS or immunosuppressive therapy.</li>
<li>Poor Hygiene: Inadequate cleanliness can increase the risk of infections leading to abscesses.</li>
<li>Invasive Procedures: Such as injections or catheter placements.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-clinical-presentation">4. Clinical Presentation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-clinical-presentation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Localized Symptoms:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Redness and Swelling: The area around the abscess may appear red and swollen.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Pain: Often severe, especially as the abscess increases in size.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Warmth: The skin over the abscess may feel warm to the touch.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Systemic Symptoms:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Fever: May be present if the infection is severe or systemic.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Malaise: General feeling of illness or fatigue.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Skin Findings:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Pustule: A visible, swollen lump filled with pus, which may eventually rupture and drain.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<ol start="5">
<li>Diagnosis</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Clinical Examination: Diagnosis is often based on physical examination and patient history. The presence of a painful, swollen lump is indicative of an abscess.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Laboratory Tests:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Blood Tests: To check for signs of systemic infection, such as elevated white blood cell count (leukocytosis) and elevated C-reactive protein (CRP).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Culture and Sensitivity: If the abscess is drained, pus can be cultured to identify the causative organism and determine appropriate antibiotic therapy.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Imaging:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Ultrasound: Useful for identifying the presence and extent of an abscess, especially in soft tissues.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ CT scan or MRI: May be used for deeper or internal abscesses to assess size, location, and potential involvement of adjacent structures.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Nursing management</p>
<ul>
<li>☑ Warm Compresses: May be used to help promote drainage and alleviate pain.</li>
<li>☑ Pain Management: Over-the-counter pain relievers such as acetaminophen or ibuprofen may be used to manage discomfort.</li>
<li>☑ Administer prescribed antibiotics: Broad-spectrum antibiotics are often started based on common pathogens until culture results are available. Targeted Therapy: Adjusted based on culture results.</li>
</ul>
<p>Surgical Intervention:</p>
<ul>
<li>Incision and Drainage: The primary treatment for an abscess involves making an incision to drain the pus. This helps relieve pressure, reduce infection, and promote healing.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Local Anesthesia: Typically used for minor abscesses.</li>
<li>Sterile Technique: Ensures that the procedure is done safely to avoid further infection.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="complications">Complications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Recurrent Abscesses: May occur if the infection is not fully treated or if there is an underlying condition that predisposes to recurrent infections.</li>
<li>Cellulitis: Spread of infection to the surrounding skin and deeper tissues.</li>
<li>Septicemia: If the infection spreads to the bloodstream, leading to systemic infection and sepsis.</li>
<li>Organ Involvement: In cases of deep abscesses, such as intra-abdominal or liver abscesses, there may be complications involving nearby organs.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="8-prevention">8. Prevention<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#8-prevention" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Hygiene Practices:</li>
<li>Wound Care: Proper cleaning and care of cuts and wounds to prevent infection.</li>
<li>Hand Hygiene: Regular hand washing and use of hand sanitizers.</li>
<li>Infection Control: Sterile Techniques: During medical procedures to prevent introduction of pathogens., Avoid Sharing Personal Items: Such as towels and razors, especially with someone who has an active infection.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="fluid-and-electrolyte-imbalance">FLUID AND ELECTROLYTE IMBALANCE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#fluid-and-electrolyte-imbalance" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Fluid Imbalance: Refers to an abnormality in the amount of body fluid.</p>
<p>It can be characterized by either an excess or deficiency of fluid in the body.</p>
<p>Electrolyte Imbalance: Refers to abnormal levels of electrolytes (sodium, potassium, calcium, magnesium, chloride, bicarbonate) in the blood. Electrolytes are crucial for many bodily functions including nerve impulse transmission, muscle contraction, and maintaining fluid balance.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="fluids-compartments">FLUIDS COMPARTMENTS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#fluids-compartments" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="total-body-water">Total Body Water<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#total-body-water" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Total Body Water (TBW) refers to the total volume of water contained in the human body.</p>
<p>It constitutes a significant part of body weight approximately 50-70% of body weight, depending on age, sex, and body composition.</p>
<p>It is generally higher in infants and decreases with age.</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>5</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>It is essential for various physiological functions, including temperature regulation, nutrient transport, and waste removal.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="components-of-tbw">Components of TBW:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#components-of-tbw" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="a-intracellular-fluid-icf">a) Intracellular Fluid (ICF):<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-intracellular-fluid-icf" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>volume: About 60% of total body water, which is approximately two-thirds of the body's water content.</li>
<li>Functions: Contains water inside cells, crucial for maintaining cell shape, metabolism, and function.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="b-extracellular-fluid-ecf">b) Extracellular Fluid (ECF):<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-extracellular-fluid-ecf" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Volume: About one-third of the body's total water.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="subdivisions-of-ecf">Subdivisions of ECF<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#subdivisions-of-ecf" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Interstitial Fluid: Surrounds cells and facilitates nutrient exchange and waste removal.</li>
<li>Intravascular Fluid(plasma): Found in blood vessels; plays a role in blood pressure regulation and transportation of cells and nutrients.</li>
<li>Transcellular Fluid: Includes specialized fluids such as cerebrospinal fluid, synovial fluid, and pleural fluid</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="physiological-importance-of-tbw-total-body-water-body-fluids">Physiological Importance of TBW, total body water (body fluids)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#physiological-importance-of-tbw-total-body-water-body-fluids" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Regulation of Body Temperature: Water helps in temperature regulation through sweating and evaporation.</li>
<li>Nutrient and Waste Transport: Facilitates the movement of nutrients into cells and the removal of waste products from cells to excretory organs.</li>
<li>Maintaining Blood Pressure: Contributes to blood volume and pressure regulation through intravascular fluid.</li>
<li>Cell Function: Essential for maintaining cell hydration, shape, and function.</li>
<li>Acid-Base Balance: Helps buffer the body's pH through various physiological processes.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="fluid-balance-mechanisms">FLUID BALANCE MECHANISMS:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#fluid-balance-mechanisms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Fluid balance in the body is crucial for maintaining homeostasis.</p>
<p>This balance involves several mechanisms and regulatory systems as described below;</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="1-fluid-loss-and-intake">1) Fluid Loss and Intake<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-fluid-loss-and-intake" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Fluid Intake: Maintained through drinking fluids and consuming food. Metabolic processes also generate water (metabolic water).</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Fluid Loss: Occurs through urine, sweat, respiration, and feces. The body monitors these losses and adjusts fluid intake and retention accordingly.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="ii-kidney-function">ii) Kidney Function<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ii-kidney-function" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The kidneys play a central role in regulating fluid balance through:</p>
<ul>
<li>☑ Filtration: Blood is filtered in the glomeruli, forming a filtrate that enters the renal tubules.</li>
<li>☑ Reabsorption: Essential substances and water are reabsorbed in the proximal tubule, loop of Henle, distal tubule, and collecting ducts, primarily regulated by hormones like ADH and aldosterone.</li>
<li>☑ Excretion: Excess fluids and waste products are excreted as urine. The kidneys can adjust urine volume and concentration based on hydration status.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="ii-fluid-distribution">ii) Fluid Distribution<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ii-fluid-distribution" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Compartments: Body fluids are distributed between intracellular (inside cells) and extracellular (outside cells) compartments. The movement of fluids between these compartments is primarily influenced by osmotic and hydrostatic pressures.</li>
<li>Osmosis: Water moves across cell membranes from areas of lower solute concentration (hypotonic) to higher solute concentration (hypertonic), helping to equalize solute concentrations.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="iii-regulatory-hormones">iii) Regulatory Hormones<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#iii-regulatory-hormones" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Several hormones play key roles in fluid balance:</p>
<ul>
<li>Antidiuretic Hormone (ADH): Released from the posterior pituitary gland in response to increased plasma osmolality (concentration of solutes). Promotes water reabsorption in the kidneys, reducing urine output and concentrating urine.</li>
<li>Aldosterone: Produced by the adrenal cortex in response to low blood volume or low sodium levels. Increases sodium reabsorption in the kidneys, leading to water retention and increased blood volume.</li>
<li>Natriuretic Peptides (ANP and BNP) Released by the heart in response to increased blood pressure or volume. Promote excretion of sodium and water, counteracting the effects of ADH9 anti diuretic hormone) and aldosterone. Atrial Natriuretic Peptide (ANP) is a hormone produced by the atria of the heart. It plays a crucial role in regulating blood pressure and fluid balance. Brain Natriuretic Peptide (BNP) is a hormone produced primarily by the ventricles of the heart in response to excessive stretching of heart muscle cells. It plays a vital role in cardiovascular health and fluid balance</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="iv-thirst-mechanism">iv) Thirst Mechanism<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#iv-thirst-mechanism" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>The thirst center in the hypothalamus responds to changes in plasma osmolality and blood volume:</p>
<ul>
<li>Increased Osmolality: Stimulates thirst, prompting fluid intake to dilute solutes.</li>
<li>Decreased Blood Volume: Also triggers thirst and can be influenced by baroreceptors that detect changes in blood pressure.</li>
</ul>
<p>v) Starling Forces</p>
<p>Fluid movement between blood vessels and interstitial spaces is influenced by:</p>
<ul>
<li>Hydrostatic Pressure: The pressure exerted by fluid in blood vessels that pushes fluid out into tissues.</li>
<li>Osmotic Pressure: The pressure exerted by proteins (especially albumin) in the blood that pulls fluid back into the bloodstream.</li>
</ul>
<p>TYPES OF FLUID IMBALANCES</p>
<p>A. HYPOVOLEMIA (FLUID DEFICIT): Decrease in the volume of extracellular fluid (ECF).</p>
<p>Causes:</p>
<p>☑ Inadequate Intake: Not drinking enough fluids.
☑ Excessive Loss: Vomiting, diarrhea, diuretics, excessive sweating.
☑ Third-Spacing: Fluid shift to interstitial or third spaces (e.g., ascites).</p>
<p>Symptoms:</p>
<p>☑ Thirst: Initial symptom.
☑ Dry Mucous Membranes: Mouth, lips, and throat.
☑ Decreased Urine Output: Oliguria (low urine output).
☑ Hypotension: Low blood pressure.
☑ Tachycardia: Increased heart rate.
☑ Skin Turgor: Decreased skin elasticity.
☑ Confusion or Lethargy: Due to reduced blood flow to the brain.</p>
<p>B. HYPERVOLEMIA (FLUID EXCESS)</p>
<p>Increase in the volume of extracellular fluid.</p>
<p>Causes:</p>
<p>☑ Excessive Intake: Overhydration, excessive intravenous fluids.
☑ Impaired Fluid Removal: Renal failure, heart failure, liver cirrhosis.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="electrolytes">ELECTROLYTES:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#electrolytes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="662c25ba">1. Sodium (Na⁺)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#662c25ba" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Normal Range: 135–145 mEq/L</p>
<p>Sodium is the primary extracellular cation and helps regulate fluid balance, blood pressure, and nerve and muscle function</p>
<p><strong>Functions:</strong></p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Regulates fluid balance and blood pressure.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Essential for nerve impulse transmission and muscle function.</p>

<ul>
<li>Table salt, processed foods, soups, and pickled foods.</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="64975889">2. Potassium (K⁺)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#64975889" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>

<p>Potassium is the primary intracellular cation and is crucial for maintaining cellular function, including nerve impulses and muscle contractions.</p>
<p><strong>Functions:</strong></p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="71062470">5. <p>Chloride is the primary extracellular anion and helps maintain fluid balance and acid-base balance.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="ecf4d11f">6. Bicarbonate (HCO₃⁻)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ecf4d11f" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Normal Range: 22–28 mEq/L</p>
<p>Bicarbonate is a key component of the buffering system that maintains the pH balance of the blood.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="functions">Functions:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#functions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>✓ Acts as a buffer to maintain acid-base balance in the body.</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Helps regulate blood pH levels.</p>
<p>Sources:</p>
<ul>
<li>Produced by the body; dietary sources include fruits and vegetables</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="7-phosphate-po4-3">7. Phosphate (PO4^3-):<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7-phosphate-po4-3" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Normal Range: 0.8-1.5 mmol/L</p>
<p>Phosphate plays a role in energy production, bone health, and cellular function.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="other-important-parameters">Other Important Parameters:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#other-important-parameters" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><strong>Osmolality:</strong> Normal Range: 275-295 mOsm/kg</p>
<p>Osmolality measures the concentration of solutes in blood and reflects the body's fluid balance and hydration status.</p>
<p><strong>Blood Volume:</strong> Normal Range: Approximately 5-6 liters for an adult, constituting about 7-8% of total body weight.</p>
<p><strong>Urine Output</strong> - Normal Range: 800-2000 mL/day. Urine output varies based on fluid intake, hydration status, and kidney function.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types-of-intravenous-fluids">TYPES OF INTRAVENOUS FLUIDS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-intravenous-fluids" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="a-hypotonic-iv-fluids">a) Hypotonic IV Fluids<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-hypotonic-iv-fluids" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Examples:</p>
<ul>
<li>0.45% Sodium Chloride (1/2 NS)</li>
<li>0.33% Sodium Chloride (1/3 NS)</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Mode of Action:</strong> Hypotonic fluids have a lower concentration of solutes compared to the plasma in the body. When administered, these fluids move into the cells via osmosis, causing the cells to swell as water is drawn in.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="indications">Indications:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#indications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>To treat cellular dehydration (e.g., in patients with hyperglycemic states like diabetic ketoacidosis).</li>
<li>To provide free water for renal excretion.</li>
<li>To correct hypernatremia (high sodium levels).</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="b-isotonic-iv-fluids">b) Isotonic IV Fluids<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-isotonic-iv-fluids" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Examples:</p>
<ul>
<li>0.9% Sodium Chloride (Normal Saline)</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Lactated Ringer's Solution</li>
<li>Dextrose 5% in Water (D5W) (initially isotonic)</li>
</ul>
<p>Mode of Action: Isotonic fluids have the same osmolarity as plasma, which means they do not cause significant movement of water into or out of the cells. They help maintain the overall fluid balance in the extracellular space.</p>
<p><strong>Indications:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>To maintain hydration.</li>
<li>To restore fluid volume in cases of blood loss, dehydration, or surgery.</li>
<li>To dilute medications for IV administration.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>c) Hypertonic IV Fluids</strong></p>
<p><strong>Examples:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>3% Sodium Chloride</li>
<li>5% Dextrose in 0.9% Sodium Chloride</li>
<li>Dextrose 10% in Water</li>
</ul>
<p>Mode of Action: Hypertonic fluids have a higher concentration of solutes than plasma. When administered, they draw water out of cells and into the extracellular space, causing cells to shrink.</p>
<p><strong>Indications:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>To treat hyponatremia (low sodium levels).</li>
<li>To reduce cerebral edema (swelling in the brain).</li>
<li>To provide nutrition in certain circumstances (e.g., high dextrose solutions).</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>ELECTROLYTE IMBALANCES</strong></p>
<p><strong>SODIUM IMBALANCE</strong></p>
<p><strong>HYPONATREMIA (LOW SODIUM)</strong></p>
<p>Hyponatremia is a condition characterized by an abnormally low concentration of sodium in the blood, less than 135 milliequivalents per liter (mEq/L)</p>
<p><strong>Causes of Hyponatremia:</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>Excessive Water Intake:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Polydipsia: Excessive water consumption, often due to psychological conditions or habit.</li>
<li>Excessive Fluid Administration: Large volumes of intravenous fluids, especially hypotonic solutions.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>
<p>Syndrome of Inappropriate Antidiuretic Hormone (SIADH): Excess ADH: Excessive release of antidiuretic hormone causes the kidneys to retain water, diluting sodium levels.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Hypovolemic Hyponatremia:</p>
</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>☑ Renal Losses: Conditions such as adrenal insufficiency or diuretic use lead to sodium loss exceeding water loss.</li>
<li>☑ Gastrointestinal Losses: Vomiting, diarrhea, or excessive sweating can cause sodium loss.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="4">
<li>Hypervolemic Hyponatremia:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>☑ Heart Failure: Congestive heart failure leads to fluid overload with dilutional hyponatremia.</li>
<li>☑ Cirrhosis: Liver disease causes fluid retention and dilution of serum sodium.</li>
<li>☑ Nephrotic Syndrome: Kidney disease with significant proteinuria and fluid retention.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="5">
<li>Euvolemic Hyponatremia:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>☑ SIADH: Despite normal blood volume, excessive ADH leads to fluid retention and dilutional hyponatremia.</li>
<li>☑ Hypothyroidism: Low thyroid hormone levels can affect fluid balance and sodium levels.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="6">
<li>Medications: Certain drugs like SSRIs, antiepileptics, and chemotherapeutics can induce hyponatremia.</li>
<li>Renal Impairment: Acute or chronic kidney disease can affect sodium regulation.</li>
</ol>
<p>SYMPTOMS OF HYPONATREMIA:</p>
<ol>
<li>Neurological Symptoms:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>☑ Headache: Common, often due to cerebral edema.</li>
<li>☑ Confusion and Disorientation: Cognitive changes due to low sodium affecting brain function.</li>
<li>☑ Seizures: Severe hyponatremia can lead to seizures.</li>
<li>☑ Coma: In extreme cases, reduced consciousness or coma may occur.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="2">
<li>General Symptoms:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>☑ Nausea and Vomiting: Common early symptoms.</li>
<li>☑ Muscle Cramps and Weakness: Result from imbalances in electrolytes affecting muscle function.</li>
<li>☑ Fatigue: General feeling of tiredness or lack of energy.</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on
5
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Severe Symptoms:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>☑ Respiratory Distress: Due to cerebral edema and fluid overload.</li>
<li>☑ Psychiatric Symptoms: Altered mental status, agitation, or hallucinations.</li>
</ul>
<p>Diagnosis of Hyponatremia:</p>
<ol>
<li>Laboratory Tests:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>☑ Serum Sodium Level: Measurement of sodium concentration in the blood.</li>
<li>☑ Serum Osmolality: Helps differentiate between true hyponatremia and pseudohyponatremia (due to elevated lipids or proteins).</li>
<li>☑ Urine Sodium Level: Elevated in cases of SIADH or hypervolemia; low in hypovolemic hyponatremia.</li>
<li>☑ Urine Osmolality: High in SIADH, low in hypovolemic hyponatremia.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="2">
<li>Clinical Evaluation:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>☑ Patient History: Identification of symptoms, recent fluid intake, medication use, and underlying conditions.</li>
<li>☑ Physical Examination: Checking for signs of fluid overload, dehydration, or neurological impairment.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="3">
<li>Further Diagnostic Tests:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>☑ Thyroid Function Tests: To rule out hypothyroidism.</li>
<li>☑ Adrenal Function Tests: To assess for adrenal insufficiency.</li>
<li>☑ Imaging Studies: May be needed to evaluate underlying conditions contributing to hyponatremia.</li>
</ul>
<p>Management of Hyponatremia:</p>
<ol>
<li>Fluid Restriction: Initial Management: Restricting fluid intake to reduce further dilution of sodium.</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Severity-Based Restrictions: More severe cases may require stricter fluid limits.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="2">
<li>Sodium Replacement:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Oral Sodium: Mild cases may be treated with oral sodium supplements.</li>
<li>Intravenous Sodium: Severe cases may require hypertonic saline (e.g., 3% NaCl) administered slowly to correct sodium levels.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="4">
<li>Address Underlying Causes:</li>
</ol>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Treatment of Primary Conditions: Managing conditions like heart failure, liver disease, or kidney disorders contributing to hyponatremia.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hypernatremia-high-sodium">HYPERNATREMIA (HIGH SODIUM)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hypernatremia-high-sodium" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Hypernatremia is a condition characterized by an abnormally high concentration of sodium in the blood, greater than 145 milliequivalents per liter (mEq/L).</p>
<ul>
<li>Causes of Hypernatremia:</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Inadequate Water Intake:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Dehydration: Insufficient fluid intake relative to the body's needs, especially in individuals who cannot access or are unable to drink enough fluids.</li>
<li>Unconscious or Confused Patients: Individuals who cannot respond to thirst or who are unconscious may not drink enough fluids.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="2">
<li>Excessive Sodium Intake:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>High-Sodium Diet: Consuming foods or beverages with excessively high sodium content.</li>
<li>Excessive Use of Sodium-Containing Medications: Overuse of sodium-containing medications or intravenous fluids with high sodium content.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="3">
<li>Loss of Free Water:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Diabetes Insipidus (DI): A condition characterized by the inability of the kidneys to concentrate urine, leading to excessive water loss.</li>
<li>Hyperglycemia: High blood glucose levels can lead to osmotic diuresis, increasing sodium concentration as water is lost.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="4">
<li>Renal Dysfunction:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Chronic Kidney Disease: Impaired kidney function can reduce the ability to excrete sodium and maintain fluid balance.</li>
<li>Acute Kidney Injury: Sudden loss of kidney function affecting sodium regulation.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="5">
<li>Hyperaldosteronism: Primary Hyperaldosteronism (Conn’s Syndrome): Excessive production of aldosterone causes sodium retention and potassium loss.</li>
<li>Excessive Sodium Retention: Cushing’s Syndrome: Excessive cortisol production can lead to sodium and water retention.</li>
</ol>
<p>Steroid Therapy: Prolonged use of corticosteroids can cause sodium retention.
7. Severe Burns: Loss of large amounts of fluid and electrolytes through damaged skin.</p>
<p>This document is available on
5 studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ol start="8">
<li>Gastrointestinal Losses: Excessive loss of water through diarrhea or vomiting, where sodium may be retained.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="symptoms-of-hypernatremia">Symptoms of Hypernatremia:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#symptoms-of-hypernatremia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="1-neurological-symptoms">1. Neurological Symptoms:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-neurological-symptoms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>☑ Thirst: The body's natural response to high sodium levels.</li>
<li>☑ Confusion and Agitation: Resulting from dehydration and hyperosmolality affecting brain function.</li>
<li>☑ Seizures: Severe hypernatremia can lead to neurological disturbances including seizures.</li>
<li>☑ Coma: In extreme cases, due to significant brain cell dehydration.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="2-general-symptoms">2. General Symptoms:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-general-symptoms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>☑ Dry Mouth and Thirst: Common symptoms due to dehydration.</li>
<li>☑ Decreased Skin Turgor: Loss of skin elasticity due to fluid loss.</li>
<li>☑ Fatigue: General tiredness or weakness from fluid imbalance.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="3-severe-symptoms">3. Severe Symptoms:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-severe-symptoms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>☑ Elevated Heart Rate: Potentially due to compensatory mechanisms in response to dehydration.</li>
<li>☑ Hypotension: Low blood pressure from significant fluid loss and decreased blood volume.</li>
<li>☑ Hyperthermia: Elevated body temperature due to dehydration.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis-of-hypernatremia">Diagnosis of Hypernatremia:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis-of-hypernatremia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="1-laboratory-tests">1. Laboratory Tests:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-laboratory-tests" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>☑ Serum Sodium Level: Measurement of sodium concentration in the blood.</li>
<li>☑ Serum Osmolality: Typically elevated, reflecting the high sodium concentration.</li>
<li>☑ Urine Sodium Level: May be low if the kidneys are conserving sodium, or normal/high depending on the cause.</li>
<li>☑ Urine Osmolality: Can help differentiate between different causes of hypernatremia, such as diabetes insipidus.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="2-clinical-evaluation">2. Clinical Evaluation:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-clinical-evaluation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Patient History: Review of symptoms, fluid intake, and any underlying conditions or medications.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>✓ Physical Examination: Assessment for signs of dehydration, such as decreased skin turgor and dry mucous membranes.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treatment-of-hypernatremia">Treatment of Hypernatremia:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment-of-hypernatremia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="1-fluid-replacement">1. Fluid Replacement:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-fluid-replacement" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>✓ Oral Fluids: For mild cases or when the patient is able to drink, providing fluids to correct dehydration.
✓ Intravenous Fluids: For more severe cases, isotonic fluids (e.g., normal saline) or hypotonic fluids (e.g., 0.45% saline or dextrose solutions) may be administered to gradually lower sodium levels.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="2-address-underlying-causes">2. Address Underlying Causes:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-address-underlying-causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>✓ Manage Diabetes Insipidus: If present, treatment may include desmopressin (a synthetic ADH) or other interventions.
✓ Treat Renal or Endocrine Disorders: Address any underlying conditions affecting sodium balance.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="3-sodium-correction">3. Sodium Correction:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-sodium-correction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>✓ Gradual Correction: Sodium levels should be corrected gradually to avoid rapid shifts that can lead to complications like cerebral edema.
✓ Monitoring: Regular monitoring of serum sodium levels and osmolality during treatment to ensure safe and effective correction.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="4-medications-diuretics-in-cases-where-fluid-overload-is-contributing-to-hypernatremia-diuretics-may-be-used-to-help-balance-fluids">4. Medications: Diuretics: In cases where fluid overload is contributing to hypernatremia, diuretics may be used to help balance fluids.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-medications-diuretics-in-cases-where-fluid-overload-is-contributing-to-hypernatremia-diuretics-may-be-used-to-help-balance-fluids" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="b-potassium-imbalance">B. POTASSIUM IMBALANCE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-potassium-imbalance" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="hypokalemia-low-potassium">Hypokalemia (Low Potassium)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hypokalemia-low-potassium" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>refers to a lower-than-normal concentration of potassium in the blood, t less than 3.5 milliequivalents per liter (mEq/L).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes-of-hypokalemia">Causes of Hypokalemia:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes-of-hypokalemia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Inadequate Potassium Intake: Dietary Deficiency: Insufficient intake of potassium-rich foods like bananas, oranges, and leafy greens.</li>
<li>Increased Potassium Loss:</li>
</ol>
<p>✓ Gastrointestinal Losses: Excessive vomiting, diarrhea, or use of certain laxatives can lead to significant potassium loss.</p>
